- **A1**: Version ID

Incorrect column caused Fringe Benefit Rate to be used instead of Labor Overhead Rate in calculations.  This was only incorrect for the second fiscal year (only column Q).

## Instructions

- **B2**: ARPA-H WORKBOOK INSTRUCTIONS
- **B4**: •     These instructions describe how to use this ARPA-H Standard Cost Proposal Workbook when an Other Transaction using a Resource Sharing agreement is contemplated. Proposers shall use a different Workbook for proposals that do not contemplate Resource Sharing.   These instructions do not replace or supersede the cost proposal instructions given in the solicitation or announcement.
- **B5**: •     This Workbook is to be used by both a Prime Proposer and its Subproposers. While each Proposer and Subproposer must complete the Workbook for its own organziation, the Prime may submit all Workbooks. Subproposers may submit theirs separately if they so choose.
- **B6**: •     The instructions that follow apply to the tabs that are colored; the spreadsheets within these tabs are linked together using references and formulas.  The non-colored/white tabs, such as Subproposer, Travel, etc. contain stand-alone spreadsheets that provide for expression of cost proposal details as required.  Formulas, etc. may be modified within the standalone tab spreadsheets (i.e., subproposer, consultants, travel, materials-supplies, equipment, ODC details, and expenditures by month).  You may add tabs and spreadhseets to the Workbook to clarify a proposal.
- **B7**: •     Note that, in addition to the instructions provided herein, each spreadsheet may have additional guidance and instructions on it.
- **B9**: Spreadsheets
- **B10**: All Speadsheets
- **C10**: •  DO NOT DELETE tabs, spreadsheets, or rows or columns within spreadsheets in this template.  This will damage the structure of the Workbook.  If you don't want to see a tab, row, or column, use the Hide function.
- **C11**: •  Before entering detailed proposal data, Proposers must begin with the "General" tab, where the Proposing- and the Prime organization name(s) (and other data) will be entered. Proposers then complete the "Proposer Constants" tab where a Business Type will be selected. When those are done, the unshaded cells within the tabs entitled" Labor Rates", "Phase # Costs," and "Ph # Task $ "must be filled in, followed by completion of the remaining spreadsheets (the uncolored tabs) that are included in the Workbook, as applicable.
- **C12**: •   Except for the "Total Amount" Spreadsheet and all Instructions throughout the workbook, unshaded/clear cells are for data entry.  Colored/shaded cells indicate references or formulas that should not be changed unless the reference or formula does not match the proposing organization's business rules.  If these references/formulas are changed, you must ensure the change does not affect the overall flow of the spreadsheet or workbook. There are notes throughout the Workbook to assist in data input. The "Total Amount" Spreadsheet pulls in data from all of the other spreadsheets and does not require any data input whatsoever.
- **C13**: •  When asked to select from a pick-list, choose the closest option presented.
- **C14**: •  If the Proposer needs to add a new line within any spreadsheet, that line must be added to the remaining associated speadsheets and done carefully, ensuring all appropriate formulas carry forward, and are duplicated in all like-spreadsheets. It is often easier to simply add the additional data to another complete Workbook and refer to such in the Cost Proposal write-up.
- **B16**: General Tab Spreadsheet
- **C16**: •   Complete cells D4, D5, D6, D7, E4, and E5.  (The CAGE codes and an accurate ARPA-H solicitation number are helpful.)
- **C17**: •  The "Summary of Proposed Total Costs" section of the General tab spreadsheet will self-complete as cost data is entered into the "Phase # Costs" spreadsheet(s).
- **B19**: Proposer Constants Tab Spreadsheet
- **C19**: •  Click on cell B5 of the "Proposer Constants" spreadsheet; a small arrow in the bottom right hand corner of that cell will appear. Click on that arrow and a drop-down list of several organization types will appear. Select the organization type that best describes the Proposer.  (If this selection is changed, the "ARPA-H Labor Group" and "ARPA-H Labor Category" will have to be reselected for each person the "Labor Rates" spreadsheet.)  If "Small Business" is selected, cells D5 and E5 will activate. Clicking on cell E5 causes a small arrow in the bottom right hand corner of that cell to appear. Click on that arrow, and a drop-down list of numbers appears that is used to identify the number of employees in the Proposing Organization; select the appropriate number.
- **C20**: •  Proposer Accounting Periods describe the begin/end dates for your organization's accounting periods. Complete cells C14 and C15 through H14 and H15. Do not leave a gap between accounting periods.
- **C21**: •  Change the Labels in Cells C13-H13 as the Proposer sees fit.  These labels will appear on line 6 above the Direct Labor costs FY in each of the "Phase # Costs" spreadsheets.
- **C22**: •  This Workbook provides Proposers with up to six fiscal years for each phase of their proposal, which is typically more than sufficient for ARPA-H R&D efforts.  Proposers should not use all six fiscal years or all Phase Cost spreadsheets if they are not applicable. If Proposers need more fiscal years (or accounting periods), use a second Workbook -- do not attempt to add fiscal years to this Workbook's spreadsheets.
- **B24**: Labor Rates Tab Spreadsheet
- **C24**: •   This Workbook relies heavily on the data within the "Labor Rates" spreadsheet.  This is where labor categories and labor rates that feed through to the cost details of the rest of the Workbook are listed.
- **C25**: •  Each person assigned to the R&D effort is represented under colums B-E, rows 8-31 of this spreadsheet. (The data within columns F, H, J, L, N, and P will pull through to the spreadsheets within the "Phase # Costs" spreadsheets.) Within each cell (rows 8-31) of Column E, put the full name of each person assigned to this project.  In column D, type in the Proposer's labor category for each person identified un Column E. Then, under Column B, click on cell B8 and a small arrow will appear in the bottom right corner. Click on that arrow and select from the list of ARPA-H labor groups that closest match that person's labor category/job title. Do this for each cell within column B through cell B31 for each person in Column E. Repeat the same process for Column C for the ARPA-H labor categories. (The descriptions of ARPA-H labor categories are in Cells C39-C48.)
- **C26**: •  Next, complete Cells F8-F31 (as applicable) and provide the fully loaded (all labor overheads added) base labor rate for each person, and then only the escalation rates threafter in columns G, I, K, M, and O. The spreadsheet will do all of the calculations; all of the fully loaded rates will pull through to the "Phase # Costs" spreadsheets. The only labor-related data that will need to be entered into the "Phase # Costs" spreadsheets are the number of hours for each person for each of the fiscal years that apply in each Phase.
- **C27**: •  When the Proposer's organization doesn't normally operate on an hourly rate basis (e.g., annual salary data), insert a formula in each Cell from F8 to F31 that divides the appropriate basis by the appropriate number of Full Time Equivalent (FTE) labor hours (for example: = [annual salary]/1,920, or 1,840); etc. (1,920 allows for 10 federal holidays and 80 hours of leave; 1,840 allows for the holidays and 4 weeks of leave).)  This formula will derive the hourly rate needed. It only needs to be done once, in the base year's labor rate fields.
- **C28**: •  If more lines for personnel are needed than the 24 provided, see the instructions below to add more lines to the "Labor Rates"sheet and the "Phase # Costs" sheets.
- **B30**: Phase # Cost Tabs Spreadsheets
- **C30**: •  Do not change the labor categories or names of personnel on the "Phase # Costs" spreadsheets.  All of those changes must be done on the "Labor Rates" spreadsheet.
- **C31**: •  The labor categories and personnel names that appear in columns A, B, and C of each "Phase # Costs" spreadsheet come from columns D and E of the "Labor Rates" spreadsheet.  All "Phase # Costs" spreadsheets should have the same personnel listed in Rows 8-31.  For example, if you have a particular person who will only be involved during Phase 2, that person's name should be listed on all "Phase # Costs" spreadsheets, but will have hours and associated costs showing only within the "Phase 2 Costs" spreadsheet.
- **C32**: •  Proposers may add additional specific cost categories (Subproposer, ODC types, etc.) as needed but must ensure those new cost categories track to the "Total Amount" spreadsheet.  Add more rows as necessary, but ensure that all formulas carry forward.
- **B34**: ADDING ROWS
- **B35**: •     This spreadsheet is designed to handle the addition of rows only; not the addition or removal of columns.  Use the Hide function to hide rows or columns that are not needed.
- **B36**: •     When adding rows to a spreadsheet, it must be done consistently for all related sheets.  In the event more than the 24 rows provided for labor categories is needed, it is best to simply add those personnel and their associated data and costs to a new Workbook.  If, however, you want to add people to the "Phase # Costs" sheets, you must begin with the "Labor Rates" sheet, where you will click on any of the rows between 8 and 31, insert the number of lines needed, copy the formulas from the row above the added line(s), paste them into the new row(s), and add the requested data. You must do the same for each of the "Phase # Costs" sheets and the "Total Amount" spreadsheet. If done correctly, all of the data within the "Labor Rates" sheet will be automatically pulled in to the "Phase # Costs" sheets, which will then transfer to the "Total Amount" sheet.

## General

- **B2**: GENERAL INFORMATION
- **B4**: Proposer Name:
- **D4**: Name
- **G4**: Proposer's CAGE Code
- **B5**: Prime Proposer:
- **D5**: Name
- **G5**: Prime's CAGE Code
- **B6**: Solicitation No.
- **D6**: Number
- **B7**: Proposer's Proposal ID:
- **D7**: ID
- **C9**: GENERAL INFORMATION
- **C10**: The information acquired by this Workbook will assist government personnel in performing their review and evaluation of the cost proposals submitted by Proposers, and will assist with negotiations should they take place.  Providing adequate supporting data and attachments, and establishing reasonableness of proposed costs, is solely the responsibility of Proposers; therefore, it is in each Proposer’s best interest to submit a fully supportable and well-prepared cost proposal, to include the basis of and rationale for all proposed costs, so the information provided can be relied upon as being current, complete, and accurate.
- **C12**: In addition to providing detailed cost summaries by Phase, each Proposer must provide a breakdown of costs by the Tasks identified in the statement of work. The "Ph # Task $" tabs provide the spreadsheets (sheets) needed to capture this data. The sum of all costs for each Task sheet (Cells M59 and N58 of each Ph # Task $" sheet) must equal the total cost summary identified in yellow (Cell O61), which is being pulled from Cell AD79 of that Phase's "Phase # Costs" sheet.
- **C13**: Any Phase that is not priced will not be included in any resulting award.
- **C14**: •   Enter the proposed cost detail in the "Phase # Costs" sheets for each Phase that applies to your proposal.  The tab entitled "Total Amount" will automatically calculate from the figures entered into the "Phase" sheets.
- **C16**: •   Before entering data in any "Phase # Costs" sheet, the non-highlighted/white fields on the "General", "Proposer Constants", and "Labor Rates" sheets must be completed.  A business type on the "Proposer Constants" sheet must be selected before "Labor Groups" and "Labor Categories" can be selected in "Labor Rates" sheet.
- **C17**: •  Proposers may add additional specific cost categories (Subproposers, ODC types, etc.) as needed but must ensure those new cost categories track to the "Total Amount" sheet.  See the Instructions tab for details.
- **C18**: •  Unshaded/White cells are for data entry.  Highlighted cells indicate references or formulas that should not be changed unless the formula does not match the Proposer's business rules.  If these formulas are changed, the Proposer must ensure the change does not affect the overall flow of the Workbook.
- **C19**: •  Ensure all costs from other sheets are correct.
- **C20**: •  If a row, column, or sheet in this Workbook is not needed for your proposal, either ignore it or hide it; do not delete it.
- **C22**: Summary of Proposed Total Costs. This chart will automatically fill in from the "Total Amount" sheet.
- **J22**: ARPA-H is interested in your feedback. If you have suggestions for improving this Workbook, please send an e-mail to elizabeth.fuller@arpa-h.gov
- **D23**: `='Total Amount'!B32`
- **E23**: `='Total Amount'!X32`

## Proposer Constants

- **B2**: PROPOSER DATA THAT AFFECTS THE WORKBOOK
- **B4**: Proposer's Business Type:
- **D4**: Small Business Size Estimate:
- **B5**: Large Business
- **C5**: Cell B4 is a drop-down-list. Click on cell B4 and the arrow at the bottom right end of the cell will activate. Choose from the drop-down list that appears. If "Small Business" is chosen, cells D4 and E4 will activate.
- **D5**: 1000+
- **E5**: This is a drop-down list. Click on Cell D4 and the arrow at the bottom right end of the cell will activate. Choose from the drop-down list that appears.
- **B11**: Proposer Accounting Periods
- **B12**: Enter the expected date range of each accounting period from the Proposer's perspective.  A period represents a change in hourly- or indirect cost rates.
- **B13**: Proposer's Preferred Label (modify):
- **C13**: FY 1
- **D13**: FY 2
- **E13**: FY 3
- **F13**: FY 4
- **G13**: FY 5
- **H13**: FY 6
- **B14**: Fiscal Year Begins Date:
- **C14**: 2025-06-01 00:00:00
- **D14**: `=EDATE(C14,12)`
- **E14**: `=EDATE(D14,12)`
- **F14**: `=EDATE(E14,12)`
- **G14**: `=EDATE(F14,12)`
- **H14**: `=EDATE(G14,12)`
- **B15**: Fiscal Year Ends Date:
- **C15**: 2026-05-31 00:00:00
- **D15**: `=EDATE(C15,12)`
- **E15**: 2028-05-31 00:00:00
- **F15**: `=EDATE(E15,12)`
- **G15**: `=EDATE(F15,12)`
- **H15**: `=EDATE(G15,12)`
- **B17**: Note 1 - A "Fiscal Year Begins Date" should be one day after the "Fiscal Year Ends Date" of the prior fiscal year (or accounting period). Cells will turn red if this condition is not met.
- **B18**: Note 2 - Proposers should put the period of performance for each Phase in cell C2 of each "Phase # Costs" sheet.

- **B34**: Instructions:
- **C34**: • If the rates have been approved/negotiated by a government agency, provide a copy of the memorandum/agreement (FPRA/FPRR). | • If the rates have not been approved/negotiated, provide sufficient detail to enable a determination of allowability, allocability and reasonableness of the allocation bases and how the rates are calculated. This information can be provided in your cost volume or add another worksheet tab in this spreadsheet to show calculations. | • If composite rates are used, provide the calculations used in deriving the composite rates in your cost volume or add another worksheet tab in this spreadsheet to show calculations.                                                                                                                                                                        | • If an FPRA is not available, provide back-up documentation for labor rates (e.g., current payroll records)
- **B35**: Note 1:
- **C35**: You must have set the Organization's "Business Type" on the Proposer Constants worksheet to populate the list of ARPA-H Labor Categories
- **B36**: Note 2:
- **C36**: Each proposed Proposer Labor Category must be associated with an ARPA-H Labor Category (columns B and C above). Choose the best fit using the descriptions below. Proposer's should then place their own labor category title and name of proposed personnel as they normally would (columns D and E above).
- **C38**: Labor Category Level
- **D38**: Description
- **C39**: Junior
- **D39**: Entry-level/Junior
- **C40**: Mid
- **D40**: Mid-level/Journeyman
- **C41**: Senior
- **D41**: Senior Level
- **C42**: Principal
- **D42**: Team Lead/Subject Matter Expert
- **C44**: Description Definitions
- **D44**: Consider experience, education, and expertise when selecting a labor category level.
- **C45**: JUNIOR
- **D45**: The junior-level or entry-level position assists more senior positions and may perform tasks and duties under supervision. This level performs work that requires practical experience and training, and applies fundamental concepts, processes, practices, and procedures on technical assignments.
- **C46**: MID
- **D46**: The journeyman or mid-level position usually performs tasks and duties independently. This position displays and applies intermediate expertise in several complex work assignments which may require originality, innovation, or independent thinking to accomplish. The journeyman or mid-level position contributes to deliverables and performance metrics and is afforded some flexibility to develop or design methods, processes, or solutions to problems.
- **C47**: SENIOR
- **D47**: The senior-level position works on high-visibility or mission-critical aspects of programs or projects and performs tasks and duties independently. This position may oversee or supervise or be responsible for the work of subordinate or less senior positions assigned to programs or projects. The senior-level position displays and applies mastery or distinguished expertise in critical tasks and high-impact assignments. This position leads, manages, plans, and functions as the technical or subject matter expert across multiple programs or projects.
- **C48**: PRINCIPAL
- **D48**: The Principal position leads or manages the entire program or project. The Principal is often a person who is considered to be a leader in a scientific or technical field.

- **A89**: Note 1: •  All cells that are clear/not highlighted should be completed by the Proposer.
- **A90**: Note 2  •  Replace the “X” in X-Months in Cell AC/AD6 with the total number of months for this Phase.

The Proposer must identify labor hours (columns E, I, M, Q, U, and Y) based on its time periods under each Direct Labor Fiscal Year. (Dates are pulled from the Proposer Constants tab.)

## Ph 1 Task $

- **B2**: Phase 1 - COST BY TASK
- **H2**: Instructions:
- **I2**: •	Insert the Tasks that you listed in the TDD Template and number appropriately. Complete all cells that are unshaded. | •	Ensure the quarter start/end dates align with your inputs in the SOW Template. - **A83**: Note 1:
- **B83**: Any proposed personnel in the technical proposal should be identified with their labor category.
- **A84**: Note 2:
- **B84**: The Fiscal Years or time periods (Row 5) are defined on the Proposer Constants tab.  The months during the period of performance that these rates apply (Row 6) are also defined on the Proposer Constants tab.
- **A85**: Note 3:
- **B85**: The values under Total Direct Labor "Hours" column indicate the total level of effort for the project for each labor category.  The Proposer must define the split of hours between initial and subsequent rate years based on its time periods defined on the Proposer Constants tab.
- **A86**: Note 4:
- **B86**: Profit or fee is not allowed on direct costs for equipment, government entities, or cost/share arrangements

- **A75**: Instructions:
- **B75**: •  For PRIME submission - Subproposer Name: If there are subproposers, list all subpropsers names. | •  In upper right last column, replace the “X” in X-Months with actual number of months. | •  Add descriptions in Column B if costs are entered in the following areas:  Fringe Benefits, Labor Overhead, Other Direct Costs (other types), Material Handling, General and Administrative, and Facilities Cost of Money. | •  Subproposers/Interorganizational Transfers: If appropriate, place Subproposer name(s) or Interorganizational Name/Code in Column B. |
- **A76**: Note 1:
- **B76**: Any proposed personnel in the technical proposal should be identified with their labor category.
- **A77**: Note 2:
- **B77**: The Fiscal Years or time periods (Row 5) are defined on the Proposer Constants tab.  The months during the period of performance that these rates apply (Row 6) are also defined on the Proposer Constants tab.
- **A78**: Note 3:
- **B78**: The values under Total Direct Labor "Hours" column indicate the total level of effort for the project for each labor category.  The Proposer must define the split of hours between initial and subsequent rate years based on its time periods defined on the Proposer Constants tab.
- **A79**: Note 4:
- **B79**: Profit or fee is not allowed on direct costs for equipment, government entities, or cost/share arrangements

- **A75**: Instructions:
- **B75**: •  For PRIME submission - Subproposer Name: If there are subproposers, list all subcontractor names. | •  In upper right last column, replace the “X” in X-Months with actual number of months. | •  Add descriptions in Column B if costs are entered in the following areas:  Fringe Benefits, Labor Overhead, Other Direct Costs (other types), Material Handling, General and Administrative, and Facilities Cost of Money. | •  Subproposers/Interorganizational Transfers: If appropriate, place Subproposer name(s) or Interorganizational Name/Code in Column B. |
- **A76**: Note 1:
- **B76**: Any proposed personnel in the technical proposal should be identified with their labor category.
- **A77**: Note 2:
- **B77**: The Fiscal Years or time periods (Row 5) are defined on the Proposer Constants tab.  The months during the period of performance that these rates apply (Row 6) are also defined on the Proposer Constants tab.
- **A78**: Note 3:
- **B78**: The values under Total Direct Labor "Hours" column indicate the total level of effort for the project for each labor category.  The Proposer must define the split of hours between initial and subsequent rate years based on its time periods defined on the Proposer Constants tab.
- **A79**: Note 4:
- **B79**: Profit or fee is not allowed on direct costs for equipment, Government entities or cost share contracts.

The Proposer must identify labor hours (columns E, I, M, Q, U, and Y) based on its time periods under each Direct Labor Fiscal Year. (Dates are pulled from the Proposer Constants tab.)

## Subproposer

- **B2**: SUBPROPOSER COST DATA
- **G2**: `=General!D4`
- **B3**: Subproposal – A fully disclosed cost proposal including support documentation will be required to be submitted by all prime or subproposers. Subproposal MS Excel cost proposal spreadsheets may be submitted directly to the government by the proposed subproposer.
- **B5**: The prime Proposer should perform and provide a cost/price analysis of each Subproposer’s cost proposal. Proposers are required to obtain competition to the maximum extent practicable when selecting Subproposers; if the Proposer has obtained competitive quotes, copies should be provided.  If the Proposer has selected other than the low bid for inclusion in its proposal or intends to award the subaward on a sole-source basis, the Proposer should provide rationale for its decision. For sole-source subawards, the prime Proposer must provide a short sole-source justification.
- **B8**: Subproposer
- **G8**: Subproposer CAGE Code
- **I8**: Competitive or Sole Source
- **K8**: Cost/price analysis included (Y/N)
- **M8**: Type of Subaward (e.g., Fixed Price, Cost plus Fixed Fee, Time and Materials, etc.)
- **O8**: Competitive Quotes (or Sole Source Documentation) Included? (Y/N)

## Consultants

- **B2**: CONSULTANTS
- **E2**: `=General!D4`
- **B5**: Instructions:
- **C5**: For the Prime - fill out all columns if applicable. Add rows as needed, ensuring the formulas in columns F, G, H, and I capture the added rows. Indicate “Not Applicable” in column C when there is no information to include.

- **C6**: Describe how and why the consultant was selected.

## Travel

- **C2**: `=General!D4`
- **E2**: TRAVEL
- **B4**: Instructions:
- **C4**: •  Provide allowable travel costs related to the performance of the agreement under the Federal Travel Regulations, prescribed by the General Services Administration.
- **C5**: •  When completing the “Origin” and “Final” Destination information, enter the city and state where travel will originate and end. For example, from Seattle WA to Washington DC. Do not list airport codes.
- **C6**: •  Include the trip purpose. It must be referred to in the Technical Proposal. Publications, conference attendance, and presentations are encouraged but must be justified to and approved by the Program Officer.
- **C7**: •  There is always one more travel day than hotel nights.
- **C8**: •  The first day and the last day of travel are charged at 75% of the M&IE per diem rate. If you travel for just one day (lasting 12 hours or more), the M&IE per diem rate is also charged at 75%. For answers to FAQs about per diem and travel rates, please review: https://www.gsa.gov/travel/plan-book/per-diem-rates/frequently-asked-questions-per-diem.
- **C9**: •  Do not combine categories.
- **C10**: •  For lodging and M&IE, use federal Per Diem Rates found at https://www.gsa.gov.
- **C11**: •  Submit backup for airfare and rental cars. Price airfare at economy rates; indicate if the airfare is refundable.
- **B12**: Note 1:
- **C12**: Estimates and the resultant costs claimed must conform to the applicable federal cost principles.
- **B13**: Note 2:
- **C13**: If there are miscellaneous expenses associated with the trip, provide description and rationale below. Add rows as needed.

- **C20**: • Fill out all columns on the Materials/Supplies Tab for each item.
- **C21**: • Add additional rows if needed. Ensure formulas are accurately captured.
- **C22**: • Include supporting documentation for each entry with an aggregate cost over $5,000. Backup may consist of an vendor quote, past purchase order/invoice, information from a website, or a detailed explanation of labor and material costs for custom made items.
- **C23**: • Clearly label Materials/Supplies backup with a Reference Document Number in the format of MAT### starting with MAT001. Place the Reference Document Number in the upper right hand side of the backup page. If there are several quoted items on a page, items not desired must be lined out and each desired item must have a separate reference number placed to the left of the item on the backup page. The Reference Document Number must be listed next to the appropriate item on the Materials/Supplies worksheet under the Reference Document Number column.
- **C24**: • Ensure that descriptions and entities listed on the Materials/Supplies worksheet match information provided in the backup.
- **C25**: • Number Reference Document Numbers sequentially so they match the Item number in Phase 1. For example, Item number 1 should match MAT001. If the same items are used again in subsequent Phases, there is no need to renumber or add additional copies of the backup, but list the items sequentially for each Phase by Reference Document Number. As an example, MAT004 could be used for Item 4 in Phase 1, Item 2 in Phase 2, Item 1 in Phase 3, etc.
- **B27**: Note 1:
- **C27**: Material is property that may be incorporated into or attached to a deliverable end item or that may be consumed or expended in performing an agreement.  It includes assemblies, components, parts, raw and processed materials, and small tools and supplies that may be consumed in normal use in performing an agreement. Material should be proposed separately from Equipment (see following spreadsheet and definitions).
- **B28**: Note 2:
- **C28**: Include a separate section in the above table for each Phase.  Add additional lines labeled needed, and ensure formulas are captured accurately.
- **B29**: Note 3:
- **C29**: In an attachment, provide all supporting documentation to support your price basis, e.g. copy of vendor quote, past invoice/PO, page from catalog, or method used for deriving engineering estimates.

Link the justification to the type of equipment purchase, i.e. special test equipment, special tooling, or plant equipment.
- **C23**: •  Include supporting documentation for each entry with aggregate cost over $5,000. Backup may consist of a vendor quote, past purchase order or invoice, information from a website, or a detailed explanation of labor and material costs for custom made items.
- **C24**: •  Label equipment backup clearly with a Reference Document Number in the format of EQ### starting with EQ001. Place the Reference Document Number in the upper right hand side of the backup page. If there are several quotes on a page, items not desired must be lined out and each desired item must have a separate reference number placed to the left of the item on the backup page. The Reference Document Number must be listed next to the appropriate item on the Equipment worksheet under the Reference Document Number column.

- **B27**: Note:
- **C27**: In an attachment, provide all supporting documentation to support your price basis, e.g. copy of quote, page from catalog, or method used for deriving engineering estimates.
- **B66**: Note 1:
- **C66**: The Government may allow equipment and/or facilities under special circumstances. If equipment and/or facilities are proposed, the specific description should identify the component, nomenclature, and configuration of the equipment/hardware that the proposer proposes to purchase for this effort.  The purchase on a direct reimbursement basis of equipment that is not included in a deliverable item will be evaluated for allowability on a case-by-case basis.  Maximum use of Government integration, test, and experiment facilities is encouraged.
- **B69**: Note 2:
- **C69**: Include a separate section in the above table for the Phase 1 and Phase 2.  Add additional lines labeled with Options if needed.
- **B71**: Note 3:
- **C71**: Definitions:
- **C72**: Special Test Equipment is defined as either single or multipurpose integrated test units engineered, designed, fabricated, or modified to accomplish special purpose testing in performing an agreement.  It consists of items or assemblies of equipment including standard or general purpose items or components that are interconnected and interdependent so as to become a new functional entity for special testing purposes.
- **C75**: Special tooling is defined as jigs, dies, fixtures, molds, patterns, taps, gauges, and all components of these items, including foundations and similar improvements necessary for installing special test equipment, and which are of such a specialized nature that without substantial modification or alteration their use is limited to the development or production of particular supplies or parts thereof or to the performance of particular services.
- **C79**: Plant equipment means personal property of a capital nature (including equipment, machine tools, test equipment, furniture, vehicles, and accessory and auxiliary items) for use in manufacturing supplies, in performing services, or for any administrative or general plant purpose. It does not include special tooling or special test equipment.
- **B82**: Note 4:
- **C82**: In an attachment, provide all supporting documentation to support your price basis, e.g. copy of vendor quote, past invoice/PO, page from catalog, or method used for deriving engineering estimates.
